    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17144064712620847477">Twenty three years ago Vivian Stanshall died in a fire, trapped in a north London flat. Drunk, he slept through his own death.<br/> <br/>Vivian was the ineffable, unflappable, elegant and irreverently funny frontman and songwriter for the Bonzo Dog Dada Band, a group of art students who’d created a band unlike any other band one could name - and still adored by thousands long after </span>
  <span id="freeText17144064712620847477" style="display:none">Twenty three years ago Vivian Stanshall died in a fire, trapped in a north London flat. Drunk, he slept through his own death.<br /> <br />Vivian was the ineffable, unflappable, elegant and irreverently funny frontman and songwriter for the Bonzo Dog Dada Band, a group of art students who’d created a band unlike any other band one could name - and still adored by thousands long after their short time in the sun was knocked on the head by Vivian himself. "We were art students. We were Dada. We were making fun of the worst excesses of rock 'n roll. One day I looked around to discover we'd become what we were parodying." <br /> <br />Written by his wife of 18 years, an artist in her own right, this is a behind-the-scenes, beneath-the-sheets, under the bed tale of an actual genius – few who admired him would disagree. In many ways this is Vivian through his own private words gleaned from his personal journals. It’s also full of up close and revealing portraits of legends: Keith Moon, John Lennon, Paul McCartney, Jimi Hendrix, George Harrison, Steve Winwood, Stephen Fry, Michael Palin, John Peel, Joe Cocker, and so many more. But even more than all that, it’s an ART BOOK: crammed full of Vivian’s paintings, sketches, unpublished family photos, letters and poems.<br /><br />Vivian Stanshall was the last of the true Bohemians. This is also a tale of Dada, a mad sad glad voyage through life on a grand scale made by one of England’s greatest treasures: the genius who was Vivian Stanshall.<br /><br />(As Ki writes: all memory is Kurosawa's "Rashomon". These are her memories accompanied by Vivian's actual journals.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17144064712620847477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16394280841032768658">I cannot wait for this book. I've been a rabid Vivian Stanshall fan since forever. Illustrations, paintings, his own journal, and his wife's great writing. A knock-out combo.<br/><br/>An update on May 16th, 2018: The book finally came and I finally read it. It's all I hoped it would be and MORE. It's a masterpiece. And now I know my hero as well as you can know someone you've never met. Longfellow's portrait is honest and loving and insightful. I cried in the end. Not true. I bawled. If possible, I love V</span>
  <span id="freeText16394280841032768658" style="display:none">I cannot wait for this book. I've been a rabid Vivian Stanshall fan since forever. Illustrations, paintings, his own journal, and his wife's great writing. A knock-out combo.<br /><br />An update on May 16th, 2018: The book finally came and I finally read it. It's all I hoped it would be and MORE. It's a masterpiece. And now I know my hero as well as you can know someone you've never met. Longfellow's portrait is honest and loving and insightful. I cried in the end. Not true. I bawled. If possible, I love Vivian Stanshall even more.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10872872130361201919">The best voice to come out of Great Britain finally gets a real book? And his missus pens it? I've read her work, all of it.   <span id="freeText10872872130361201919" style="display:none">The best voice to come out of Great Britain finally gets a real book? And his missus pens it? I've read her work, all of it. Who said (something like): Lucky is the man who gets a good biographer. Though she says this isn't a biography or a memoir. How intriguing. It's full of the great man's work? Paintings, sketches, etchings. I am atremble. I have all his albums. I still listen to his solo work because his solo work is timeless, especially that prodigious genius displayed throughout the spoken Sir Henry at Rawlinson End. Add all this to Ki Longfellow's poetic understanding and I itch to get my hands on a copy. I wonder if I can bear to review it? I'll find out. First in line, me. Oh, and I've forced my friends to listen to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1070672.Vivian_Stanshall" title="Vivian Stanshall" rel="nofollow noopener">Vivian Stanshall</a> too. Some don't get it, but a lot do. I'm thinking of culling friends based on how they respond to "Strange Tongues", one of the greatest songs ever written.<br /><br />UPDATE: An incredible work of art about an artist by an artist. All I hoped for and MORE. Intense love.</span>

<div id="review_2308168755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2308168755" />
    <a title="Ira Robbins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15838062-ira-robbins"><img alt="Ira Robbins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600955227p2/15838062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2308168755?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ira Robbins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ira Robbins" href="/user/show/15838062-ira-robbins">Ira Robbins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2308168755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10774005711450701888">This is a truly extraordinary memoir of "Mr. Standstill" by the woman who knew him best. The writing is affectionate, insightful and clear-eyed, capturing the man's genius while making no effort to smooth over his messy life. <br/><br/>It is very odd to read an interview one did in 1979, and which one can scarcely recall beyond its occurrence, narrated in prose, but that is typical of the book's achievement -- to bring the distant past very much back to life. <br/><br/>The loosely structured -- but extremely deep a</span>
  <span id="freeText10774005711450701888" style="display:none">This is a truly extraordinary memoir of "Mr. Standstill" by the woman who knew him best. The writing is affectionate, insightful and clear-eyed, capturing the man's genius while making no effort to smooth over his messy life. <br /><br />It is very odd to read an interview one did in 1979, and which one can scarcely recall beyond its occurrence, narrated in prose, but that is typical of the book's achievement -- to bring the distant past very much back to life. <br /><br />The loosely structured -- but extremely deep and detailed -- story of Vivian's life as well as Ki's is revealing, illuminating and highly entertaining, despite the tragedy and disappointments strewn throughout. Packed with family photographs as well as Vivian's art and pointed new illustrations by Ben Wickley, this is a must for anyone to whom the phrases "English eccentric" or "Bonzo Dog" ring a thrilling note.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10774005711450701888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jase" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77379450-jase"><img alt="Jase" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2285152313?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jase" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jase" href="/user/show/77379450-jase">Jase</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285152313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15569558421945911668">I've waited for this book for so long I thought it couldn't be what I hoped it would be. It is! It's much more than I hoped for. Pictures and paintings I'd never seen, Vivian's own words from his private journals, horrible things, wonderful things, warts and bruises and kisses. I cried a lot. I laughed a lot. I read certain things over and over to make sure I understood what his wife was saying. As for his wife, the woman who wrote the book she promised him, he was a lucky bloke. So many reasons</span>
  <span id="freeText15569558421945911668" style="display:none">I've waited for this book for so long I thought it couldn't be what I hoped it would be. It is! It's much more than I hoped for. Pictures and paintings I'd never seen, Vivian's own words from his private journals, horrible things, wonderful things, warts and bruises and kisses. I cried a lot. I laughed a lot. I read certain things over and over to make sure I understood what his wife was saying. As for his wife, the woman who wrote the book she promised him, he was a lucky bloke. So many reasons to say this but the one I think of now is to have his portrait painted by an artist of her ability. The language is sometimes poetic, always clever, and her understanding of the man she was with is way beyond the usual biographer. As she says this is not a biography and she's right. It isn't but it also is. I came away loving my hero more. Vivian was a tragic figure, a beautiful soul, and a destructive mess. He changed my life in so many ways. This book told me how and why and who. It's also a daring look at the nature of the artist and of art. Brilliant brilliant book. 10 stars. (Forgot to mention the extraordinary work of her illustrator. Pure delight.)</span>

<div id="review_2129168039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2129168039" />
    <a title="Nathaniel Fox" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71638091-nathaniel-fox"><img alt="Nathaniel Fox" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518721125p2/71638091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2129168039?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathaniel Fox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathaniel Fox" href="/user/show/71638091-nathaniel-fox">Nathaniel Fox</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71638091-nathaniel-fox?shelf=vivian-stanshall">vivian-stanshall</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71638091-nathaniel-fox?shelf=surrealism">surrealism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71638091-nathaniel-fox?shelf=bonzo-dog-band">bonzo-dog-band</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2129168039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5739508741901131136">To begin with, the writing is stunning. Depending on what is being described or discussed, it is poetic, transcendent, informative, funny, enlightening, and deeply understanding of its subject which is of course the genius who was Vivian Stanshall. No wonder he called Longfellow his "translator". It might have taken her too long to understand alcoholism, but it took her no time at all to recognize his brilliance. What she didn’t recognize was her own. But Vivian did. She allowed herself to becom</span>
  <span id="freeText5739508741901131136" style="display:none">To begin with, the writing is stunning. Depending on what is being described or discussed, it is poetic, transcendent, informative, funny, enlightening, and deeply understanding of its subject which is of course the genius who was Vivian Stanshall. No wonder he called Longfellow his "translator". It might have taken her too long to understand alcoholism, but it took her no time at all to recognize his brilliance. What she didn’t recognize was her own. But Vivian did. She allowed herself to become subservient to his varied and astonishing talent. As I read along, I saw that he, in turn, was secretly subservient to her talent. His pride kept this from her until just before his death. By then, she was doing no more than waiting. She still believed he'd choose life. If he had, I don't imagine this book would ever exist. They'd have too much still to do together to bother looking back.<br /><br />I've read quite a few biographies, a handful of memoirs, but I've read nothing like this. Many close to such brilliance as Vivian's simply describe what happened on this day or that. (In Vivian's case a repetition of his so-called zaniness.) Not Longfellow. She describes inner truths, deep and surprising insights, sad memories of sad moments, glad memories of glad moments. She understands what he lived for, what mattered to him. As an artist herself, she understood his drive, his obsession. She understands Art. That's what we're being given here: the mystery of the born artist through the life and death of one sublime artist.<br /><br />All in all, it's a love story of surpassing sadness and beauty. <br /><br />There's also what I consider a clever and telling use of the Akira Kurosawa's film "Rashomon". In Rashomon all tell their own story and all the stories are different. There is no one truth. This book is Longfellow's truth. But she adds so many other truths, different voices, even those who disagree with her, never claiming hers is the final say. Vivian himself has his own say in language meant only for himself. His say is surely none of those who love him would ever expect to hear coming from the master of language. He stands revealed by his own simple words.<br /><br />Aside from all these "truths we are being given as a great gift, there is also all the paintings, the sketches Longfellow saved, the carvings, the images of the things he loved, gorgeous photos I've never seen before, and the truly exceptional illustrations of Ben Wickey, a very young artist who is very old in his ability and his insight. What Wickey has done would no doubt delight Vivian down to his unusual toes. There are things Vivian would adore. A model of the Thekla (the Stanshall's magical ship that launched not only itself but prodigious talent of every kind), a flip book, a page of paper dolls (oh how I wish I could deface my copy to cut them out!), a double image of Vivian to color - the book seems unending in its visual invention. If nothing else, and I can't believe anyone would see nothing else, the book doing no more than lying on a table will make any room explode with color and interest. <br /><br />If you're looking for a pop bio, perhaps this book is not your cuppa tea. For one thing it's much too beautiful… just as he was. But if you love Vivian, if he changed your life, if you want to reach out and touch the real man (so much is gleaned from his private journals, no lying, no trying to impress, just a man's naked soul) then any price is worth this magnificent book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5739508741901131136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2382422895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4399271398260184028">I read this book only because Ki Longfellow wrote it. I had no idea who her husband was. I do now. This is exactly what I would expect from Longfellow. Truthful, revealing, funny, sad, wonderfully constructed, brilliantly written, and a complete joy to read. And to look at. It's stuffed with all sorts of images. The illustrator, Ben Wickey, is a talent to be on the look out for. The whole book is quite literally a masterpiece. (It also made me search for Vivian Stanshall. I came away with two re</span>
  <span id="freeText4399271398260184028" style="display:none">I read this book only because Ki Longfellow wrote it. I had no idea who her husband was. I do now. This is exactly what I would expect from Longfellow. Truthful, revealing, funny, sad, wonderfully constructed, brilliantly written, and a complete joy to read. And to look at. It's stuffed with all sorts of images. The illustrator, Ben Wickey, is a talent to be on the look out for. The whole book is quite literally a masterpiece. (It also made me search for Vivian Stanshall. I came away with two reactions. As an Englishman I am ashamed not to know this great English artist. I am now listening to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6839613.Sir_Henry_at_Rawlinson_End" title="Sir Henry at Rawlinson End by Vivian Stanshall" rel="nofollow noopener">Sir Henry at Rawlinson End</a> and I've bought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2396377.Stinkfoot" title="Stinkfoot by Vivian Stanshall" rel="nofollow noopener">Stinkfoot</a>. After that it's Teddy Boys Don't Knit. And secondly, I thought what a tremendous couple they must have been and what a loss of such a man to Longfellow. It made me sad to think about it.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4399271398260184028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2356612667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4719498850747022885">This book says it isn't "exactly a biography or a memoir". But it is, and so much more. It's brilliantly touching, funny, unbearably sad, scathingly honest, very very clever, beautifully written, and as a "gift to her husband Vivian Stanshall" (a real genius and someone I admire with all my heart), it can't be bested. I've waited and waited for this book. Actually, before I heard his wife was writing it, I was waiting for any book to be written about him. One came out ages ago but it is so far i</span>
  <span id="freeText4719498850747022885" style="display:none">This book says it isn't "exactly a biography or a memoir". But it is, and so much more. It's brilliantly touching, funny, unbearably sad, scathingly honest, very very clever, beautifully written, and as a "gift to her husband Vivian Stanshall" (a real genius and someone I admire with all my heart), it can't be bested. I've waited and waited for this book. Actually, before I heard his wife was writing it, I was waiting for any book to be written about him. One came out ages ago but it is so far inferior to its subject it might as well not be mentioned. But I was waiting so I could know him better, understand him better, get closer to someone so rare, and sadly, so doomed. This is that book. It's a masterpiece of understanding and sympathy and honest OUCH truth. At the end I cried my heart out.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6891961487986779402">This book will break your heart. But it will also stimulate your brain, make you laugh, cause wonder at how some people give everything to life. And then there's all the art and the photos and the illustrations. Huge kudos to the young illustrator, Ben Wickey. I'll just bet he's going places. As for the writing... Vivian is a lucky Dog. He's been immortalized by his own wife, a great talent.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15952344-ledreader?shelf=bonzo-dog-band">bonzo-dog-band</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2459214113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2090609972555502650">Vivian Stanshall was a genius. Not like Stephen Fry who is merely a polymath and a second rate comic, actor and writer, Vivian was the real deal and he found his match in Ki Longfellow he was wise enough to marry. We should all be so lucky. This is a work of combined genius. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="BoBoBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111439408-bobobooks"><img alt="BoBoBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584332657p2/111439408.jpg" /></a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111439408-bobobooks?shelf=vivian-stanshall">vivian-stanshall</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111439408-bobobooks?shelf=biography">biography</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232791449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3531250798525575208">I've read quite a few biographies. Most chosen because I was already interested in the person. This is the first I've read because I am a fan of the writer and was very curious to hear how she would present her own husband, the "love of her life" who died in a fire. I was, to be truthful, stunned. Not much compares to Longfellow's truthfulness, her ability to portray another human in all his faults and all of hers. Dead impressed. Not only is this a visually beautiful book, an extraordinary read</span>
  <span id="freeText3531250798525575208" style="display:none">I've read quite a few biographies. Most chosen because I was already interested in the person. This is the first I've read because I am a fan of the writer and was very curious to hear how she would present her own husband, the "love of her life" who died in a fire. I was, to be truthful, stunned. Not much compares to Longfellow's truthfulness, her ability to portray another human in all his faults and all of hers. Dead impressed. Not only is this a visually beautiful book, an extraordinary read about artists warts and all (including hers) but it's a heartbreaking work about love overcoming all that would harm it. As soon as I read it, of course I did some research about the love of Longfellow's life. I see now. Two brilliant souls entangled in a relationship that is undying. I admit I had a few tears and a few laughs and a few thoughts about the nature of born artists clashing together like great cymbals of every emotion humans have.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3531250798525575208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6522263925759001889" style="display:none">I've actually met both Vivian and Ki. Lucky me. They were in Muswell Hill, a place I seldom visited. Still, my destiny was working well those two times. I've met other heroes but none like Vivian. I melted. Ki, no doubt used to such reactions, was wonderful to me. I've also learned through reading it three times that those two deserved each other. Like finds like. It's brilliant book. Ki knew who Vivian was and why he was. Plus she is a fabulous talent of her own. No doubt Vivian knew that. This book I shall treasure forever. More stars than five.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11551830167380094449">A remarkable book. Truthful both about its subject and its author. I've always thought Vivian Stanshall was a tragic genius in the true sense of tragic. (So sad that the word tragic is now reduced to a simple accident.) He had a fatal flaw which Longfellow finally saw so clearly and it killed him, as fatal flaws usually do. But before that happened he produced some of the finest works of painting, performing, the written word, the spoken word, songs he wrote and recorded... basically as his wido</span>
  <span id="freeText11551830167380094449" style="display:none">A remarkable book. Truthful both about its subject and its author. I've always thought Vivian Stanshall was a tragic genius in the true sense of tragic. (So sad that the word tragic is now reduced to a simple accident.) He had a fatal flaw which Longfellow finally saw so clearly and it killed him, as fatal flaws usually do. But before that happened he produced some of the finest works of painting, performing, the written word, the spoken word, songs he wrote and recorded... basically as his widow (so obviously brilliant herself - what a couple they were) said: he was a complete artist and could be nothing else. I laughed. I cried. I grieved that I never had the chance to meet him no matter what shape he was is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11551830167380094449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lGiDsXgyzGNx9Px/ZDrwoVom8tf5MpjsaI+MTH2sIWlnRhsKF8JAJ+BgH//HjA23t/ScPFj8ZL3G2g4q76MxEg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2ovGIMNpcWvzyPBl9PNSKxIBLUsQy9myXGN4UoDeAXcppV6brJn9L2JcE+VXRa89/9NDoLEFJePyNvo0EtERDA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_110737'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110737.Seabiscuit?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Seabiscuit: An American Legend<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/30913.Laura_Hillenbrand?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Laura Hillenbrand<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.21 avg rating &mdash; 146,142 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1999\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer13132509611761712914\">There\'s an alternate cover edition here\n\nSeabiscuit was one of the most electrifying and popular attractions in sports history and the single biggest newsmaker in the world in 1938, receiving more coverage than FDR, Hitler, or Mussolini. But his succ<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13132509611761712914\" style=\"display:none\">There\'s an alternate cover edition here\n\nSeabiscuit was one of the most electrifying and popular attractions in sports history and the single biggest newsmaker in the world in 1938, receiving more coverage than FDR, Hitler, or Mussolini. But his success was a surprise to the racing establishment, which had written off the crooked-legged racehorse with the sad tail. Three men changed Seabiscuit’s fortunes:Charles Howard was a onetime bicycle repairman who introduced the automobile to the western United States and became an overnight millionaire. When he needed a trainer for his new racehorses, he hired Tom Smith, a mysterious mustang breaker from the Colorado plains. Smith urged Howard to buy Seabiscuit for a bargain-basement price, then hired as his jockey Red Pollard, a failed boxer who was blind in one eye, half-crippled, and prone to quoting passages from Ralph Waldo Emerson. Over four years, these unlikely partners survived a phenomenal run of bad fortune, conspiracy, and severe injury to transform Seabiscuit from a neurotic, pathologically indolent also-ran into an American sports icon. Author Laura Hillenbrand brilliantly re-creates a universal underdog story, one that proves life is a horse race.From the Hardcover edition.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13132509611761712914\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/286014.Ki_Longfellow">About Ki Longfellow</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/286014.Ki_Longfellow"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1252801606p3/286014.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/286014.Ki_Longfellow">Ki Longfellow
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
860
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15010268771799864962">Ki Longfellow, born on Staten Island, New York, to a French-Irish mother and an Iroquois father, grew up in Hawaii and Marin County, California, but ended up living in France and England for many years. She is the widow of a British national treasure, the complete artist Vivian Stanshall.<br/><br/>In England, she created and sailed the Thekla, a 180 foot Baltic Trader, to the port of Bristol where it became</span>
  <span id="freeText15010268771799864962" style="display:none">Ki Longfellow, born on Staten Island, New York, to a French-Irish mother and an Iroquois father, grew up in Hawaii and Marin County, California, but ended up living in France and England for many years. She is the widow of a British national treasure, the complete artist Vivian Stanshall.<br /><br />In England, she created and sailed the Thekla, a 180 foot Baltic Trader, to the port of Bristol where it became the Old Profanity Showboat. It remains there today as a Bristol landmark. On it, she and Vivian wrote and staged a unique musical for the sheer joy of it. "Stinkfoot, a Comic Opera," garnered a host of delighted, if slightly puzzled, national reviews. <br /><br />Her first book, "China Blues," was the subject of a bidding war. "China Blues," and her second novel, "Chasing Women," introduced Longfellow to Hollywood... a long hard but ultimately fascinating trip. ("China Blues" was reissued by Eio Books in 2012.)<br /><br />When Vivian died in 1995, Ki stopped writing, living on Standing Room Only Farm in Vermont. Time may not heal, but it tempers. Eventually Ki began writing again, but her subject became the moment at age 19 that informed her life... a direct experience with the Divine. She chose the figure of Mary Magdalene to tell that tale in her novel "The Secret Magdalene." Nancy Savoca, a brilliant independent film maker (winner of the Sundance Grand Jury Prize with her first film, "True Love") traveled all the way to Vermont to option the book as her next film.<br /><br />Ki's second book on the Divine Feminine is "Flow Down Like Silver," a novel about the numinous and gifted Hypatia of Alexandria, a tragically ignored historical figure of towering intellect who searched through intellect for what the Magdalene knew in her heart.<br /><br />In a huge departure from her all she'd written before, Longfellow found herself weaving a tale of supernatural horror called "Houdini Heart." This book was selected by the Horror Writers of America as one of a handful of books to be considered for their 2011 Bram Stoker Award for Best Horror Novel.<br /><br />In the Spring of 2013 the first three titles of her Sam Russo noir murder mystery series was published by Eio Books: "Shadow Roll," "Good Dog, Bad Dog," and "The Girl in the Next Room." There is a fourth title "Dead on the Rocks" available and there may be more. Or maybe not.<br /><br />In December, 2013, she released a tale of one woman's attempt to survive lost in the Sonoran Desert: "Walks Away Woman." <br /><br />She’s at work on the third and last book in her Divine Feminine series. Meant to be one thing, it's become quite another thing. Writers may think they know what they're going to write, but they can be very wrong. This book is "The White Bee".<br /><br />In late January of 2018 she published the art book, biography, and memoir she'd promised Vivian Stanshall she would one day write for him: "The Illustrated Vivian Stanshall, a Fairytale of Grimm Art".<br /><br />in the early months of 2018 three more of her books were optioned for Hollywood, one as a high end television mini-series and two as films.<br /><br />She lives wherever she finds herself. Currently that’s between Somerset, England and Olympia, Washington.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15010268771799864962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
